scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Summer&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</div></th><td>\n<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+1</span> (<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">British Summer Time</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date format</th><td>\ndd/mm/yyyy&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">Driving side</a></th><td>\nleft</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_the_Isle_of_Man" class="mw-redirect" title="Telephone numbers in the Isle of Man">Calling code</a></th><td>\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">\n<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background:transparent;text-align:left;font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom#Isle_of_Man" title="Telephone numbers in the United Kingdom">+44</a></div>\n<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">Landlines:<br />+441624<br />Mobiles:<br />+447524<br />+447624<br />+447924\n  </li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:IM" title="ISO 3166-2:IM">IM</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/.im" title=".im">.im</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_footnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_footnote_a">^</a></b></span>  The Manx pound is in parity with the pound sterling, and is only legal tender in the Isle of Man.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Isle of Man</b> (<a href="/wiki/Manx_language" title="Manx language">Manx</a>: <i lang="gv">Ellan Vannin</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Manx" title="Help:IPA/Manx">[\xcb\x88\xc9\x9bl\xca\xb2\xc9\x99n \xcb\x88van\xc9\xaan]</a></span>), sometimes referred to simply as <b>Mann</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Manx_language" title="Manx language">Manx</a>: <i lang="gv">Mannin</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Manx" title="Help:IPA/Manx">[\xcb\x88man\xc9\xaan]</a></span>),  is a self-governing British <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependency</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> between <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, who holds the title of <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_Mann" title="Lord of Mann">Lord of Mann</a> and is represented by a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Lieutenant Governor of the Isle of Man">Lieutenant Governor</a>. Defence is the responsibility of the United Kingdom.\n</p><p>Insurance and <a href="/wiki/Online_gambling" title="Online gambling">online gambling</a> generate 17% of <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross national product">GNP</a> each, followed by <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">information and communications technology</a> and banking with 9% each.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island has been inhabited since before 6500 BC. <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaelic</a> cultural influence began in the 5th century AD, and the <a href="/wiki/Manx_language" title="Manx language">Manx language</a>, a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Gaelic languages</a>, emerged. In 627, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_of_Northumbria" title="Edwin of Northumbria">Edwin of Northumbria</a> conquered the Isle of Man along with most of <a href="/wiki/Mercia" title="Mercia">Mercia</a>. In the 9th century, <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norsemen</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Isles" title="Kingdom of the Isles">Kingdom of the Isles</a>. <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Barefoot" title="Magnus Barefoot">Magnus III</a>, King of Norway, was King of Mann and the Isles between 1099 and 1103.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1266, the island became part of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scotland</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Perth" title="Treaty of Perth">Treaty of Perth</a>, after being ruled by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Norway">Norway</a>. After a period of alternating rule by the kings of Scotland and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a>, the island came under the feudal lordship of the <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">English Crown</a> in 1399. The lordship <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Purchase_Act_1765" title="Isle of Man Purchase Act 1765">revested</a> into the British Crown in 1765, but the island never became part of the 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> or its successors the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a> and the present-day <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. It retained its internal self-government.\n</p><p>In 1881, the Isle of Man <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a>, became the first national <a href="/wiki/Legislative_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative body">legislative body</a> in the world to give <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women&#39;s suffrage">women the right to vote</a> in a general election, but this excluded married women.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the Isle of Man was awarded <a href="/wiki/World_Network_of_Biosphere_Reserves" title="World Network of Biosphere Reserves">biosphere reserve status</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a tocsection-26"><a href="#Language"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Language</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Symbols"><span folklore</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">10.5</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Food"><span class="tocnumber">10.6</span> <span class="toctext">Food</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">10.7</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-33"><a href="#Motorcycle_racing"><span class="tocnumber">10.7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Motorcycle racing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-34"><a href="#Cammag"><span class="tocnumber">10.7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cammag</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Cinema"><span class="tocnumber">10.8</span> <span class="toctext">Cinema</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Fauna"><span class="tocnumber">10.9</span> <span class="toctext">Fauna</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Manx name of the Isle of Man is <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Ellan Vannin</i></i>: <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">ellan</i></i> (<small>Manx pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Manx" title="Help:IPA/Manx">[\xc9\x9bl\xca\xb2\xc9\x99n]</a></span>) is a Manx word meaning \'island\'; <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Mannin</i></i> (<small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Manx" title="Help:IPA/Manx">[man\xc9\xaan]</a></span>) appears in the <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive case</a> as <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Vannin</i></i> (<small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Manx" title="Help:IPA/Manx">[van\xc9\xaan]</a></span>), with <a href="/wiki/Consonant_mutation#Celtic_languages" title="Consonant mutation">initial consonant mutation</a>, hence <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Ellan Vannin</i></i>, "Island of Mann".  The short form often used in English, Mann, is derived from the Manx <i>Mannin</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> though sometimes the name is written as Man. The earliest recorded Manx form of the name is <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Manu</i></i> or <i><i lang="gv" title="Manx language text">Mana</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Old_Irish" title="Old Irish">Old Irish</a> form of the name is <i><i lang="sga" title="Old Irish language text">Manau</i></i> or <i><i lang="sga" title="Old Irish language text">Mano</i></i>. <a href="/wiki/Old_Welsh" title="Old Welsh">Old Welsh</a> records named it as <i><i lang="owl" title="Old Welsh language text">Manaw</i></i>, also reflected in <i><i lang="owl" title="Old Welsh language text"><a href="/wiki/Manaw_Gododdin" title="Manaw Gododdin">Manaw Gododdin</a></i></i>, the name for an ancient district in north Britain along the lower <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Koch2006_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koch2006-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\nThe oldest known reference to the island calls it <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Mona</i></i>, in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, 54&#160;BC); in the 1st century AD, <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> records it as <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Monapia</i></i> or <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Monabia</i></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> (2nd century) as <i>Mon\xc5\x93da</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">M\xce\xbf\xce\xbd\xce\xb1\xce\xbf\xce\xb9\xce\xb4\xce\xb1</span>, <i>Monaoida</i>) or <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">M\xce\xbf\xce\xbd\xce\xb1\xcf\x81\xce\xb9\xce\xbd\xce\xb1</span> (<i>Monarina</i>), in <a href="/wiki/Koine_Greek" title="Koine Greek">Koine Greek</a>.\nLater Latin references have <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Mevania</i></i> or <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">M\xc3\xa6navia</i></i> (<a href="/wiki/Orosius" title="Orosius">Orosius</a>, 416),<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\nand <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Eubonia</i></i> or <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Eumonia</i></i> by Irish writers. It is found in the <a href="/wiki/Sagas_of_Icelanders" title="Sagas of Icelanders">Sagas of Icelanders</a> as <i><i lang="is" title="Icelandic language text">M\xc3\xb6n</i></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name is probably cognate with the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> name of the island of <a href="/wiki/Anglesey" title="Anglesey">Anglesey</a>, <i><i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text">Ynys M\xc3\xb4n</i></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Koch2006_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koch2006-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\nusually derived from a <a href="/wiki/Insular_Celtic_languages" title="Insular Celtic languages">Celtic</a> word for \'mountain\' (reflected in Welsh <i><i lang="cy" title="Welsh language text">mynydd</i></i>, <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a> <i><i lang="br" title="Breton language text">menez</i></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> <i><i lang="gd" title="Scottish Gaelic language text">monadh</i></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\nfrom a <a href="/wiki/Proto-Celtic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Celtic">Proto-Celtic</a> <i>*moniyos</i>.\n</p><p>The name was at least secondarily associated with that of <a href="/wiki/Manann%C3%A1n_mac_Lir" title="Manann\xc3\xa1n mac Lir">Manann\xc3\xa1n mac Lir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Irish_mythology" title="Irish mythology">Irish mythology</a> (corresponding to Welsh <i><i lang="owl" title="Old Welsh language text"><a href="/wiki/Manawydan" title="Manawydan">Manawydan</a> fab Ll\xc5\xb7r</i></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In the earliest Irish mythological texts, Manann\xc3\xa1n is a king of the <a href="/wiki/Otherworld" title="Otherworld">otherworld</a>, but the 9th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Sanas_Cormaic" title="Sanas Cormaic">Sanas Cormaic</a></i> identifies a <a href="/wiki/Euhemerism" title="Euhemerism">euhemerised</a> Manann\xc3\xa1n as "a famous merchant who resided in, and gave name to, the Isle of Man".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Later, a Manann\xc3\xa1n is recorded as the first <a href="/wiki/King_of_Mann" title="King of Mann">king of Mann</a> in a Manx poem (dated 1504).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="History of the Isle of Man">History of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg/220px-The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg/330px-The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg/440px-The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Braaid_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_21-APR-09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Braaid" title="The Braaid">The Braaid</a> in central Isle of Man, with remnants of a Celtic-Norse <a href="/wiki/Roundhouse_(dwelling)" title="Roundhouse (dwelling)">roundhouse</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Longhouse" title="Longhouse">longhouses</a>, c. AD 650\xe2\x80\x93950</div></div></div>\n<p>The island was cut off from the surrounding islands around 8000&#160;BC, and was colonised by sea some time before <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">6500&#160;BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brad8_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brad8-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The first residents were <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> and fishermen. Examples of their tools are kept at the Manx Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg/220px-Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg.png" width="220" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg/330px-Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg/440px-Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1297" data-file-height="1362" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kingdom_of_Mann_and_the_Isles-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Isles" title="Kingdom of the Isles">Kingdom of the Isles</a> about the year 1100</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> Period marked the beginning of farming, and <a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">megalithic monuments</a> began to appear, such as Cashtal yn Ard near <a href="/wiki/Maughold_(parish)" title="Maughold (parish)">Maughold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Godred_Crovan" title="Godred Crovan">King Orry</a>\'s Grave at <a href="/wiki/Laxey" title="Laxey">Laxey</a>, Meayll Circle near <a href="/wiki/Cregneash" title="Cregneash">Cregneash</a>, and Ballaharra Stones at <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s,_Isle_of_Man" title="St John&#39;s, Isle of Man">St John\'s</a>. There were also the local <a href="/wiki/Ronaldsway_culture" title="Ronaldsway culture">Ronaldsway</a> and Bann cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, burial mounds became smaller. Bodies were put in stone-lined graves with ornamental containers. The Bronze Age burial mounds created long-lasting markers around the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The ancient Romans knew of the island and called it <i><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Insula Manavia</i></i><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> although it is uncertain whether they conquered the island. Around the 5th century AD, large-scale migration from Ireland precipitated a process of <a href="/wiki/Gaelicisation" title="Gaelicisation">Gaelicisation</a> evidenced by <a href="/wiki/Ogham" title="Ogham">Ogham</a> inscriptions, giving rise to the <a href="/wiki/Manx_language" title="Manx language">Manx language</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Goidelic language</a> closely related to <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> arrived at the end of the 8th century. They established <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a> and introduced many land divisions that still exist. In 1266 <a href="/wiki/Magnus_VI_of_Norway" title="Magnus VI of Norway">King Magnus VI of Norway</a> ceded the islands to Scotland in the Treaty of Perth; but Scotland\'s rule over Mann did not become firmly established until 1275, when the Manx were defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ronaldsway" title="Battle of Ronaldsway">Battle of Ronaldsway</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Castletown,_Isle_of_Man" title="Castletown, Isle of Man">Castletown</a>.\n</p><p>In 1290 King <a href="/wiki/Edward_I_of_England" title="Edward I of England">Edward I of England</a> sent <a href="/wiki/Walter_de_Huntercombe,_1st_Baron_Huntercombe" title="Walter de Huntercombe, 1st Baron Huntercombe">Walter de Huntercombe</a> to take possession of Mann. It remained in English hands until 1313, when <a href="/wiki/Robert_the_Bruce" title="Robert the Bruce">Robert Bruce</a> took it after besieging <a href="/wiki/Castle_Rushen" title="Castle Rushen">Castle Rushen</a> for five weeks. A confused period followed when Mann was sometimes under English rule and sometimes Scottish, until 1346, when the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Neville%27s_Cross" title="Battle of Neville&#39;s Cross">Battle of Neville\'s Cross</a> decided the long struggle between England and Scotland in England\'s favour.\n</p><p>English rule was delegated to a series of lords and magnates. The <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a> passed laws concerning the government of the island in all respects and had control over its finances, but was subject to the approval of the <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_Mann" title="Lord of Mann">Lord of Mann</a>.\n</p><p>In 1866, the Isle of Man obtained limited home rule, with partly democratic elections to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Keys" title="House of Keys">House of Keys</a>, but an appointed <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Legislative Council of the Isle of Man">Legislative Council</a>. Since then, democratic government has been gradually extended.\n</p><p>The Isle of Man has designated more than 250 historic sites as <a href="/wiki/Registered_Buildings_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Registered Buildings of the Isle of Man">registered buildings</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sound_IOM.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Sound_IOM.JPG/230px-Sound_IOM.JPG" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Sound_IOM.JPG/345px-Sound_IOM.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Sound_IOM.JPG/460px-Sound_IOM.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sound_IOM.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Calf_of_Man" title="Calf of Man">Calf of Man</a> seen from <a href="/wiki/Cregneash" title="Cregneash">Cregneash</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Geography of the Isle of Man">Geography of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="List of islands of the Isle of Man">List of islands of the Isle of Man</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biota_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Biota of the Isle of Man">Biota of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>The Isle of Man is located in the middle of the northern <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a>, almost equidistant from <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> (closest), and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> (farthest). It is 52 kilometres (32&#160;mi) long and, at its widest point, 22 kilometres (14&#160;mi) wide. It has an area of around 572 square kilometres (221&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-gov.im_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov.im-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Besides the island of Mann itself, the political unit of the Isle of Man includes some nearby small islands: the seasonally inhabited <a href="/wiki/Calf_of_Man" title="Calf of Man">Calf of Man</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chicken_Rock" title="Chicken Rock">Chicken Rock</a> on which stands an unmanned lighthouse, <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Isle" title="St Patrick&#39;s Isle">St Patrick\'s Isle</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Michael%27s_Isle" title="St Michael&#39;s Isle">St Michael\'s Isle</a>. The last two of these are connected to the main island by permanent roads/causeways.\n</p><p>Ranges of hills in the north and south are separated by a central valley. The northern plain, by contrast, is relatively flat, consisting mainly of deposits from glacial advances from western Scotland during colder times. There are more recently deposited <a href="/wiki/Shingle_beach" title="Shingle beach">shingle beaches</a> at the northernmost point, the <a href="/wiki/Point_of_Ayre" title="Point of Ayre">Point of Ayre</a>. The island has one mountain higher than 600 metres (2,000&#160;ft), <a href="/wiki/Snaefell" title="Snaefell">Snaefell</a>, with a height of 620 metres (2,034&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-gov.im_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov.im-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> According to an old saying, from the summit one can see six kingdoms: those of Mann, Scotland, England, Ireland, Wales, and <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">Heaven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Some versions add a seventh kingdom, that of the sea, or <a href="/wiki/Neptune_(mythology)" title="Neptune (mythology)">Neptune</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Bundling_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim has too many footnotes for reading to be smooth. (October 2017)">excessive citations</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg/230px-Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg.png" width="230" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg/345px-Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg/460px-Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_Man_map-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Isle of Man</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Manx_people" title="Manx people">Manx people</a></div>\n<p>At the 2016 census,<sup id="cite_ref-Census2016_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2016-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> the Isle of Man was home to 83,314 people, of whom 26,997 resided in the island\'s <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douglas,_Isle_of_Man" title="Douglas, Isle of Man">Douglas</a> and 9,128 in the adjoining village of <a href="/wiki/Onchan" title="Onchan">Onchan</a>. The population decreased by 1.4% between the 2011 and 2016 censuses. By country of birth, those born in the Isle of Man were the largest group (49.8%), while those born in the United Kingdom were the next largest group at 40% (33.9% in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, 3% in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, 2% in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> and 1.1% in Wales), 1.8% in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> and 0.75% in the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>. The remaining 8.5% were born elsewhere in the world, with 5% coming from EU countries (other than the UK and Ireland).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Census">Census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <i>Isle of Man Full Census</i>, last held in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> has been a decennial occurrence since 1821, with interim censuses being introduced from 1966. It is separate from, but similar to, the <a href="/wiki/Census_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Census in the United Kingdom">Census in the United Kingdom</a>.\n</p><p>The 2001 census was conducted by the Economic Affairs Division of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Treasury" title="Isle of Man Treasury">Isle of Man Treasury</a>, under the authority of the Census Act 1929.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Isle of Man has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen</a> <i>Cfb</i>). Average rainfall is higher than averaged over the territory of the British Isles, because the Isle of Man is far enough from Ireland for the prevailing south-westerly winds to accumulate moisture. Average rainfall is highest at <a href="/wiki/Snaefell" title="Snaefell">Snaefell</a>, where it is around 1,900 millimetres (75&#160;in) a year. At lower levels it can be around 800 millimetres (31&#160;in) a year. The highest recorded temperature was 28.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C (84.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F) at <a href="/wiki/Ronaldsway" title="Ronaldsway">Ronaldsway</a> on 12 July 1983.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source &#35;1: <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a><sup id="cite_ref-Metoffice_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metoffice-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;">Source &#35;2: M\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9o Climat<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IoM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/IoM.jpg/280px-IoM.jpg" width="280" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/IoM.jpg/420px-IoM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/IoM.jpg/560px-IoM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="571" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IoM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A composite satellite image of the Isle of Man</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Government" title="Isle of Man Government">Isle of Man Government</a></div>\n<p>The United Kingdom is responsible for the island\'s defence and ultimately for <a href="/wiki/Good_governance" title="Good governance">good governance</a>, and for representing the island in international forums, while the island\'s own parliament and government have competence over all domestic matters.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Socio-political_structure">Socio-political structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Socio-political structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Manx_law" title="Manx law">Manx law</a></div>\n<p>The island\'s parliament, <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a>, is claimed to have been in continuous existence since 979 or earlier, purportedly making it the oldest continuously governing body in the world, though evidence supports a much later date.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Tynwald is a <a href="/wiki/Tricameralism#Isle_of_Man" title="Tricameralism">bicameral or tricameral</a> legislature, comprising the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Keys" title="House of Keys">House of Keys</a> (directly elected by universal suffrage with a voting age of 16 years) and the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Legislative Council of the Isle of Man">Legislative Council</a> (consisting of indirectly elected and <a href="/wiki/Ex_officio_member" title="Ex officio member">ex-officio members</a>). These two bodies also meet together in joint session as Tynwald Court.\n</p><p>The executive branch of government is the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Council of Ministers of the Isle of Man">Council of Ministers</a>, which is composed of members of the House of Keys. It is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Chief Minister of the Isle of Man">Chief Minister</a>, currently (2017) <a href="/wiki/Howard_Quayle" title="Howard Quayle">Howard Quayle</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_House_of_Keys" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the House of Keys">MHK</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vice-regal" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice-regal">Vice-regal</a> functions of the head of state are performed by a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Lieutenant Governor of the Isle of Man">Lieutenant Governor</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="External_relations_and_security">External relations and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: External relations and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/External_relations_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="External relations of the Isle of Man">External relations of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>In various laws of the United Kingdom, "the United Kingdom" is defined to exclude the Isle of Man. Historically, the UK has taken care of its external and defence affairs, and retains paramount power to legislate for the Island. However, in 2007, the Isle of Man and the UK signed an agreement<sup id="cite_ref-framework_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-framework-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> that established frameworks for the development of the international identity of the Isle of Man. There is no separate Manx citizenship. Citizenship is covered by UK law, and Manx people are classed as British citizens. The Isle of Man holds neither membership nor associate membership of the European Union, and lies outside the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> (EEA).There is a long history of relations and cultural exchange between the Isle of Man and Ireland. The Isle of Man\'s historic <a href="/wiki/Manx_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Manx Gaelic">Manx Gaelic</a> language (and its modern revived variant) are closely related to both Scottish Gaelic and the Irish language, and in 1947, Irish Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a> spearheaded efforts to save the dying Manx language.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence">Defence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Defence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Under <a href="/wiki/British_law" class="mw-redirect" title="British law">British law</a>, the Isle of Man is not part of the United Kingdom. However, the UK takes care of its external and defence affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> There are no independent military forces on the Isle of Man, although <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ramsey_(M110)" title="HMS Ramsey (M110)">HMS <i>Ramsey</i></a> is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Ramsey,_Isle_of_Man" title="Ramsey, Isle of Man">town of the same name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> From 1938 to 1955 there was the <a href="/wiki/Manx_Regiment" title="Manx Regiment">Manx Regiment</a> of the British <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Army_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial Army (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a>, which saw extensive action during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 1779, the <a href="/wiki/Manx_Fencible_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Manx Fencible Corps">Manx Fencible Corps</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fencible" class="mw-redirect" title="Fencible">fencible</a> regiment of three companies, was raised; it was disbanded in 1783 at the end of the <a href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a>. Later, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Manx_Fencibles" title="Royal Manx Fencibles">Royal Manx Fencibles</a> was raised at the time of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. The 1st Battalion (of 3 companies) was raised in 1793. A 2nd Battalion (of 10 companies) was raised in 1795,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and it saw action during the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rebellion_of_1798" title="Irish Rebellion of 1798">Irish Rebellion of 1798</a>. The regiment was disbanded in 1802.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> A third body of Manx Fencibles was raised in 1803 to defend the island during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> and to assist the Revenue. It was disbanded in 1811.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 a multi-capability recruiting and training unit of the <a href="/wiki/Army_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Army Reserve (United Kingdom)">British Army Reserve</a> was established in Douglas.<sup id="cite_ref-Isle_of_Man_Army_Reserve_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Isle_of_Man_Army_Reserve-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_services">Emergency services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Emergency services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Isle of Man Government maintains five emergency services.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> These are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Constabulary" title="Isle of Man Constabulary">Isle of Man Constabulary</a> (police)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Coastguard" title="Isle of Man Coastguard">Isle of Man Coastguard</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Isle of Man Fire and Rescue Service">Isle of Man Fire and Rescue Service</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Ambulance_Service" title="Isle of Man Ambulance Service">Isle of Man Ambulance Service</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Civil_Defence_Corps" title="Isle of Man Civil Defence Corps">Isle of Man Civil Defence Corps</a></li></ul>\n<p>All of these services are controlled directly by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Home_Affairs_(Isle_of_Man)" title="Department of Home Affairs (Isle of Man)">Department of Home Affairs</a> of the Isle of Man Government, and are independent of the United Kingdom. Nonetheless, the Isle of Man Constabulary voluntarily submits to inspection by the British inspectorate of police,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and the Isle of Man Coastguard contracts Her Majesty\'s Coastguard (UK) for air-sea rescue operations.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Citizenship">Citizenship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Citizenship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_man_passport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Isle_of_man_passport.jpg/220px-Isle_of_man_passport.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Isle_of_man_passport.jpg/330px-Isle_of_man_passport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Isle_of_man_passport.jpg/440px-Isle_of_man_passport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="997" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isle_of_man_passport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cover of an Isle of Man passport</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Manx_passport" class="mw-redirect" title="Manx passport">Manx passport</a></div>\n<p>Citizenship in the Isle of Man is governed by British law. Passports issued by the Isle of Man Passport Office say <i>"British Islands \xe2\x80\x93 Isle of Man"</i> on the cover but the nationality status stated on the passport is simply <i>"British Citizen"</i>. Although Manx passport holders are British citizens, because the Isle of Man is not part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, people born on the island without a parent or grandparent either born, naturalised, registered or resident for more than five consecutive years in the United Kingdom do not have the same rights as other British citizens with regard to employment and establishment in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Isle of Man passports can be issued to any British citizen in the Isle of Man (whether or not that person has "Manx status" as an Isle of Man worker under the local Isle of Man employment laws). They can also be issued to Manx-connected British citizens residing in Britain or either of the other Crown Dependencies.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Isle of Man is neither part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, nor has a <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">special status</a>, and thus did not take part in the 2016 <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">referendum</a> on the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> membership. However, Protocol 3 of the UK\'s Act of Accession to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a> included the Isle of Man within the <a href="/wiki/EU%27s_customs_area" class="mw-redirect" title="EU&#39;s customs area">EU\'s customs area</a>, allowing for trade in Manx goods without tariffs throughout the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> As it is not part of the <a href="/wiki/EU%27s_internal_market" class="mw-redirect" title="EU&#39;s internal market">EU\'s internal market</a>, there are still limitations on the movement of capital, services and labour.\n</p><p>EU citizens are entitled to travel and reside, but not work, in the island without restriction. Manx citizens\xe2\x80\x94without the hereditary qualification outlined above\xe2\x80\x94are similarly restricted from working in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The effect of the UK leaving the European Union is uncertain. The UK has confirmed that the Crown Dependencies\' position will be included in the <a href="/wiki/Brexit_negotiations" title="Brexit negotiations">Brexit negotiations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GRBWP_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GRBWP-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>ch.5</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commonwealth_of_Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Commonwealth of Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Isle of Man is not itself a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>. By virtue of its relationship with the United Kingdom, it takes part in several Commonwealth institutions, including the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Parliamentary_Association" title="Commonwealth Parliamentary Association">Commonwealth Parliamentary Association</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Isle_of_Man" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of the Isle of Man">Government of the Isle of Man</a> has made calls for a more integrated relationship with the Commonwealth,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> including more direct representation and enhanced participation in Commonwealth organisations and meetings, including Commonwealth Heads of Government Meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Chief Minister of the Isle of Man">Chief Minister of the Isle of Man</a> has said: "A closer connection with the Commonwealth itself would be a welcome further development of the island\'s international relationships."<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg/200px-IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg.png" width="200" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg/300px-IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg/400px-IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IsleOfMan_SheadingsAndParishes-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Isle of Man local authorities and <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_Isle_of_Man#Sheadings" title="Local government in the Isle of Man">sheadings</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Politics of the Isle of Man">Politics of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="List of political parties in the Isle of Man">List of political parties in the Isle of Man</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Elections in the Isle of Man">Elections in the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>Most Manx politicians stand for election as independents rather than as representatives of political parties. Although political parties do exist, their influence is not nearly as strong as in the United Kingdom.\n</p><p>There are three political parties in the Isle of Man. The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Vannin_Party" title="Liberal Vannin Party">Liberal Vannin Party</a> (established 2006) has two seats in the House of Keys; it promotes greater Manx independence and more accountability in government. The <a href="/wiki/Manx_Labour_Party" title="Manx Labour Party">Manx Labour Party</a> is the other: it held two seats in the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Council_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Legislative Council of the Isle of Man">Legislative Council</a> until 28 February 2018 when it reduced to one seat. The <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Green_Party" title="Isle of Man Green Party">Isle of Man Green Party</a> was established in 2016 but currently only has representation on a <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Local government in the Isle of Man">local government</a> level.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A number of pressure groups also exist on the island. <a href="/wiki/Mec_Vannin" title="Mec Vannin">Mec Vannin</a> advocate the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Positive_Action_Group" title="Positive Action Group">Positive Action Group</a> campaign for three key elements to be introduced into the governance of the island: open accountable government, rigorous control of public finances, and a fairer society.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Local government in the Isle of Man">Local government in the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>Local government on the Isle of Man is based partly on the island\'s 17 ancient parishes. There are two types of local authorities:\n</p>\n<ul><li>a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">corporation</a> for the Borough of Douglas, and bodies of commissioners for the town districts of <a href="/wiki/Castletown,_Isle_of_Man" title="Castletown, Isle of Man">Castletown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peel,_Isle_of_Man" title="Peel, Isle of Man">Peel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramsey,_Isle_of_Man" title="Ramsey, Isle of Man">Ramsey</a>, and</li>\n<li>the village districts of <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Michael" class="mw-redirect" title="Kirk Michael">Kirk Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onchan" title="Onchan">Onchan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Erin" title="Port Erin">Port Erin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_St_Mary" title="Port St Mary">Port St Mary</a>, and the 14 "parish districts" (those parishes or parts of parishes which do not fall within the districts previously mentioned). Each of these districts also has its own body of commissioners.</li></ul>\n<p>Local authorities are under the supervision of the Isle of Man Government\'s Department of Local Government and the Environment (DOLGE).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Demographics of the Isle of Man">Demographics of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Education in the Isle of Man">Education in the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>Public education is under the Department of Education and Children. Thirty-two primary schools, five secondary schools and the <a href="/wiki/University_College_Isle_of_Man" title="University College Isle of Man">University College Isle of Man</a> function under the department.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Health in the Isle of Man">Health in the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>Health and social care on the Isle of Man is the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_and_Social_Care_(Isle_of_Man)" title="Department of Health and Social Care (Isle of Man)">Department of Health and Social Care (Isle of Man)</a>. Healthcare is free for residents and visitors from the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Economy of the Isle of Man">Economy of the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>The Isle of Man <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Enterprise_(Isle_of_Man)" title="Department for Enterprise (Isle of Man)">Department for Enterprise</a> manages the diversified economy in 12 key sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The largest sectors by GNP are insurance and <a href="/wiki/Online_gambling" title="Online gambling">eGaming</a> with 17% of GNP each, followed by <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communications_technology" title="Information and communications technology">ICT</a> and banking with 9% each. The 2016 census lists 41,636 total employed.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The largest sectors by employment are "medical and health", "financial and business services", construction, retail and public administration.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Manufacturing, focused on aerospace and the food and drink industry,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> employs almost 2000 workers and contributes with about 5% of <a href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Domestic Product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP). The sector provides laser optics, industrial diamonds, electronics, plastics and aerospace precision engineering. Tourism, agriculture, fishing, once the mainstays of the economy, now make very little contributions to the island\'s GDP.\n</p><p>After 30 years of continued GDP growth, the unemployment rate is just around 1%.\n</p><p>The Isle of Man is a low-tax economy with no <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wealth_tax" title="Wealth tax">wealth tax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stamp_duty" title="Stamp duty">stamp duty</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">inheritance tax</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and a top rate of <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> of 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-opw_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opw-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> A tax cap is in force: the maximum amount of tax payable by an individual is \xc2\xa3125,000 or \xc2\xa3250,000 for couples if they choose to have their incomes jointly assessed. Personal income is assessed and taxed on a total worldwide income basis rather than a <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittance</a> basis. This means that all income earned throughout the world is assessable for Manx tax rather than only income earned in or brought into the island.\n</p><p>The standard rate of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporation tax</a> for residents and non-residents is 0%. Retail business profits above \xc2\xa3500,000 and banking business income are taxed at 10%, and rental (or other) income from land and buildings situated on the Isle of Man is taxed at 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg/250px-Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg" width="250" height="84" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg/375px-Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg/500px-Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3538" data-file-height="1187" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peel_-_Peel_Bay_Beach_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1719663.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peel,_Isle_of_Man" title="Peel, Isle of Man">Peel</a> is the island\'s main fishing port.</div></div></div>\n<p>Trade takes place mostly with the United Kingdom. The island is in customs union with the UK, and related revenues are pooled and shared under the <a href="/wiki/Common_Purse_Agreement" title="Common Purse Agreement">Common Purse Agreement</a>. This means that the Isle of Man cannot have the lower excise revenues on alcohol and other goods that are enjoyed in the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>.\n</p><p>The Manx government <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Film" title="Isle of Man Film">promotes island locations for making films</a> by offering financial support. Since 1995, over 100 films have been made on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Most recently the island has taken a much wider strategy to attract the general digital media industry in film, television, video and <a href="/wiki/ESports" class="mw-redirect" title="ESports">eSports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Isle of Man Government Lottery operated from 1986 to 1997. Since 2 December 1999 the island has participated in the <a href="/wiki/National_Lottery_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Lottery (United Kingdom)">United Kingdom National Lottery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The island is the only jurisdiction outside the United Kingdom where it is possible to play the UK National Lottery.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Since 2010 it has also been possible for projects in the Isle of Man to receive national lottery <a href="/wiki/The_National_Lottery_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="The National Lottery Awards">Good Causes Funding</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The good causes funding is distributed by the Manx Lottery Trust.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a> receives the 12p lottery duty for tickets sold in the island.\n</p><p>Tourist numbers peaked in the first half of the 20th century, prior to the boom in cheap travel to Southern Europe that also saw the decline of tourism in many similar English seaside resorts. The Isle of Man tourism board has recently invested in "Dark Sky Discovery" sites to diversify its tourism industry. It is expected that dark skies will generally be nominated by the public across the UK. However, the Isle of Man tourism board tasked someone from their team to nominate 27 places on the island as a civil task. This cluster of the highest quality "Milky Way" sites <sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> is now well promoted within the island. This government push has effectively given the island a headstart in the number of recognised Dark Sky sites. However, this has created a distorted view when compared to the UK where this isn\'t promoted on a national scale. There, Dark Sky sites are expected to be nominated over time by the public across a full cross section of national town, city and countryside locations rather than <i>en masse</i> by government departments.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Isle of Man is seen to be "accommodating"<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> towards <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">Bitcoin</a>, which is a growing technology on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017 an office of <a href="/wiki/The_International_Stock_Exchange" title="The International Stock Exchange">The International Stock Exchange</a> was opened to provide a boost for the island\'s finance industry.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communications_on_the_Isle_of_Man" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications on the Isle of Man">Communications on the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<p>The main telephone provider on the Isle of Man is <a href="/wiki/Manx_Telecom" title="Manx Telecom">Manx Telecom</a>. The island has two mobile operators: Manx Telecom, previously known as Manx Pronto, and <a href="/wiki/Sure_(company)" title="Sure (company)">Sure</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cloud9_(service_provider)" title="Cloud9 (service provider)">Cloud9</a> operated as a third mobile operator on the island for a short time, but has since withdrawn.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Broadband internet services are available through four local providers: Wi-Manx, Domicilium, Manx Computer Bureau and <a href="/wiki/Manx_Telecom" title="Manx Telecom">Manx Telecom</a>. The island does not have its own <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">ITU</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_country_calling_codes" title="List of country calling codes">country code</a>, but is accessed via the British country code (+44), and the island\'s telephone numbers are part of the <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Telephone numbers in the United Kingdom">British telephone numbering plan</a>, with local dialling codes 01624 for landlines and 07524, 07624 and 07924 for mobiles. Calls to the island from the UK however, are generally charged differently from those within the UK, and may or may not be included in any "inclusive minutes" packages.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1996, the Isle of Man Government obtained permission to use the <a href="/wiki/.im" title=".im">.im</a> national <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a> (TLD), and has ultimate responsibility for its use. The domain is managed from day to day by Domicilium, an island-based internet service provider.\n</p><p>In December 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Manx_Electricity_Authority" title="Manx Electricity Authority">Manx Electricity Authority</a> and its telecommunications subsidiary, e-llan Communications, commissioned the laying of a new fibre-optic link that connects the island to a worldwide fibre-optic network.\n</p><p>The Isle of Man has three radio stations: <a href="/wiki/Manx_Radio" title="Manx Radio">Manx Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_FM_(Isle_of_Man)" title="Energy FM (Isle of Man)">Energy FM</a> and <a href="/wiki/3_FM" title="3 FM">3 FM</a>.\n</p><p>There is no insular television service, but local transmitters retransmit British mainland digital broadcasts via the free-to-air <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital terrestrial">digital terrestrial</a> service <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a>. The Isle of Man is served by <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_West" title="BBC North West">BBC North West</a> for <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC Two</a> television services, and <a href="/wiki/ITV_Granada" title="ITV Granada">ITV Granada</a> for <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>.\n</p><p>Many television services are available by satellite, such as <a href="/wiki/Sky_(UK_%26_Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky (UK &amp; Ireland)">Sky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Freesat" title="Freesat">Freesat</a> from the group of satellites at <a href="/wiki/Astra_28.2%C2%B0E" title="Astra 28.2\xc2\xb0E">28.2\xc2\xb0 East</a>, as well as services from a range of other satellites around Europe such as the <a href="/wiki/SES_Astra" title="SES Astra">Astra</a> satellites at <a href="/wiki/Astra_19.2%C2%B0E" title="Astra 19.2\xc2\xb0E">19.2\xc2\xb0 east</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hotbird" class="mw-redirect" title="Hotbird">Hotbird</a>.\n</p><p>The Isle of Man has three newspapers, all weeklies, and all owned by <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Newspapers" title="Isle of Man Newspapers">Isle of Man Newspapers</a>, a division of the Edinburgh media company <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Press" title="Johnston Press">Johnston Press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Courier" title="Isle of Man Courier">Isle of Man Courier</a></i> (distribution 36,318) is free and distributed to homes on the island. The other two newspapers are <i><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Examiner" title="Isle of Man Examiner">Isle of Man Examiner</a></i> (circulation 13,276) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Manx_Independent" title="Manx Independent">Manx Independent</a></i> (circulation 12,255).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Postal services are the responsibility of <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle of Man Post">Isle of Man Post</a>, which took over from the British <a href="/wiki/General_Post_Office" title="General Post Office">General Post Office</a> in 1973.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_Isle_of_Man" title="Transport in the Isle of Man">Transport in the Isle of Man</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg/220px-Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg/330px-Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg/440px-Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_Sea_Terminal_-_Isle_of_Man_-_kingsley_-_20-APR-09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sea Terminal front fa\xc3\xa7ade</div></div></div>\n<p>There is a comprehensive bus network, operated by the government-owned bus operator <a href="/wiki/Bus_Vannin" title="Bus Vannin">Bus Vannin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Sea_Terminal" title="Isle of Man Sea Terminal">Isle of Man Sea Terminal</a> in Douglas has regular ferries to and from <a href="/wiki/Heysham" title="Heysham">Heysham</a> and to and from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, with a more restricted timetable operating in winter. There are also limited summer-only services to and from <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. The Dublin route also operates at Christmas. At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_TT" title="Isle of Man TT">Isle of Man TT</a> a limited number of sailings operate to and from <a href="/wiki/Larne_Harbour_railway_station" title="Larne Harbour railway station">Larne</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. All ferries are operated by the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Steam_Packet_Company" title="Isle of Man Steam Packet Company">Isle of Man Steam Packet Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The only commercial airport on the island is the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Airport" title="Isle of Man Airport">Isle of Man Airport</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ronaldsway" title="Ronaldsway">Ronaldsway</a>. There are direct scheduled and chartered flights to numerous airports in the United Kingdom and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the oldest operating horse tram services is located on the sea front in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Douglas,_Isle_of_Man" title="Douglas, Isle of Man">Douglas</a>. It was founded in 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-Heritage_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heritage-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island used to have an extensive narrow-gauge railway system, both steam-operated and electric, but the majority of the steam railway tracks were taken out of service many years ago, and the track removed. As of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Isle_of_Man&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there is a <a href="/wiki/Isle_Of_Man_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Isle Of Man Railway">steam railway</a> between Douglas and Port Erin, an <a href="/wiki/Manx_Electric_Railway" title="Manx Electric Railway">electric railway</a> between Douglas and Ramsey and an <a href="/wiki/Snaefell_Mountain_Railway" title="Snaefell Mountain Railway">electric mountain railway</a> which climbs <a href="/wiki/Snaefell" title="Snaefell">Snaefell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Heritage_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heritage-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The island has a total of 688 miles (1,107&#160;km)<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> of public roads, all of which are paved. There is no overriding national speed restriction; only local speed limits are set and some roads have no speed limit.
